</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>New Spain</b> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span lang="es"><i>Nueva España</i></span>) was a colonial territory of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> north of the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">Isthmus of Panama</a>. It was established following the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Aztec_Empire" title="Spanish conquest of the Aztec Empire">Spanish conquest of the Aztec Empire</a> in 1521, and following additional conquests, it was made a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_viceroyalty" title="Spanish viceroyalty">viceroyalty</a> (Spanish: <i>virreinato</i>) in 1535. The first of four viceroyalties Spain created in the Americas, it comprised <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, much of the <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">Southwestern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_United_States" title="Central United States">Central United States</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Spanish Florida</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Philippines, Guam, Mariana and Caroline Islands</a>.</p>
<p>After 1535 the colony was governed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroy_of_New_Spain" title="Viceroy of New Spain">Viceroy of New Spain</a>, an appointed minister of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Spanish_monarchs" title="List of Spanish monarchs">King of Spain</a>, who ruled as monarch over the colony. The capital of New Spain was <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>New Spain lost parts of its territory to other European powers and independence, but the core area remained under Spanish control until 1821, when it achieved independence as the Mexican Empire— when the latter dissolved, it became modern Mexico and Central America. It developed highly regional divisions, which reflect the impact of climate, topography, the presence or absence of dense indigenous populations, and the presence or absence of mineral resources. The areas of central and southern Mexico had dense indigenous populations with complex social, political, and economic organization. The northern area of Mexico, a region of nomadic and semi-nomadic indigenous populations, was not generally conducive to dense settlements, but the discovery of silver in <a href="/wiki/Zacatecas" title="Zacatecas">Zacatecas</a> in the 1540s drew settlement there to exploit the mines. Silver mining not only became the engine of the economy of New Spain, but vastly enriched Spain, and transformed the global economy. New Spain was the New World terminus of the Philippine trade, making the viceroyalty a vital link between Spain's New World empire and its Asian empire.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_New_Spain_and_its_relationship_to_the_crown">Kingdom of New Spain and its relationship to the crown</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Kingdom of New Spain and its relationship to the crown">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_New_Spain" title="Kingdom of New Spain">Kingdom of New Spain</a> was established following the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Aztec_Empire" title="Spanish conquest of the Aztec Empire">Spanish conquest of the Aztec Empire</a> in 1521 as a New World kingdom dependent on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Spanish_monarchs" title="List of Spanish monarchs">Spanish Crown</a>, since the initial funds for exploration came from <a href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castile" title="Isabella I of Castile">Queen Isabella</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Although New Spain was a dependency of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, it was a kingdom not a colony, subject to the presiding monarch on the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haring_7_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Haring_7-5">[5]</a></sup> The monarch had sweeping power in the overseas territories,</p>
<blockquote>
<p>The king possessed not only the sovereign right but the property rights; he was the absolute proprietor, the sole political head of his American dominions. Every privilege and position, economic political, or religious came from him. It was on this basis that the conquest, occupation, and government of the [Spanish] New World was achieved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haring_7_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Haring_7-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The Viceroyalty of New Spain was established in 1535 in the Kingdom of New Spain. It was the first New World viceroyalty and one of only two in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_empire" title="Spanish empire">Spanish empire</a> until the 18th century <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Reforms" title="Bourbon Reforms">Bourbon Reforms</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Territorial_extent_of_the_overseas_Spanish_Empire">Territorial extent of the overseas Spanish Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Territorial extent of the overseas Spanish Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> comprised the territories in the north overseas 'Septentrion', from <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, to the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Philippine, Mariana and Caroline Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>At its greatest extent, the Spanish crown claimed on the mainland of the Americas, much of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> south of <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, that is: all of present-day <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a> except <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>; most of present-day <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> west of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a>, plus <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">the Floridas</a>.</p>
<p>To the west of the continent, New Spain also included the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Spanish East Indies</a> (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Islands" title="Philippine Islands">Philippine Islands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">Mariana Islands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">Caroline Islands</a>, parts of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Formosa" title="Spanish Formosa">Taiwan</a>, and parts of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moluccas" title="Moluccas">Moluccas</a>). To the east of the continent, it included the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_West_Indies" title="Spanish West Indies">Spanish West Indies</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> (comprising the modern states of <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>), <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bay_Islands_(department)" title="Bay Islands (department)">Bay Islands</a>).</p>
<p>Until the 18th century, when Spain saw its claims in North America threatened by other European powers, much of what are called the Spanish borderlands, territory now part of the United States. This was not occupied by many Spanish settlers and were considered more marginal to Spanish interests than the most densely populated and lucrative areas of central Mexico. To shore up its claims in North America starting in the late 18th century, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_expeditions_to_the_Pacific_Northwest" title="Spanish expeditions to the Pacific Northwest">Spanish expeditions to the Pacific Northwest</a> explored and claimed the coast of what is now British Columbia and Alaska. On the mainland, the administrative units included <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Californias" title="Las Californias">Las Californias</a>, that is, the Baja California peninsula, still part of Mexico and divided into <a href="/wiki/Baja_California" title="Baja California">Baja California</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Sur" title="Baja California Sur">Baja California Sur</a>; <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">Alta California</a> (present-day <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, western Colorado, and south Wyoming); (from the 1760s) <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_Spain)" title="Louisiana (New Spain)">Louisiana</a> (including the western Mississippi River basin and the Missouri River basin); <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Extremadura" title="Nueva Extremadura">Nueva Extremadura</a> (the present-day states of <a href="/wiki/Coahuila" title="Coahuila">Coahuila</a> and <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico" title="Santa Fe de Nuevo México">Santa Fe de Nuevo México</a> (parts of <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conquest_era_.281521.E2.80.931535.29">Conquest era (1521–1535)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Conquest era (1521–1535)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Conquest_of_the_Aztec_Empire" title="Spanish Conquest of the Aztec Empire">Spanish Conquest of the Aztec Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mexico_City" title="History of Mexico City">History of Mexico City</a></div>
<p>The Caribbean islands and early Spanish explorations around the circum-Caribbean region had until 1521 not been of major political, strategic, or financial importance until the conquest of the <a href="/wiki/Aztec_Empire" title="Aztec Empire">Aztec Empire</a>. However, important precedents of exploration, conquest, and settlement and crown rule had been initially worked out in the Caribbean, which long affected subsequent regions, including Mexico and Peru.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The indigenous societies of <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a> brought under Spanish control were of unprecedented complexity and wealth from what they had encountered in the Caribbean. This indigenous complexity and wealth now controlled by conquerors presented both an important opportunity and a potential threat to the power of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a>, since the conquerors were acting independent of effective crown control. The societies could provide the <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistadors</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hernán Cortés">Hernán Cortés</a>, a base from which the conquerors could become autonomous, or even independent, of the Crown.</p>
<p>As a result, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">King of Spain, Charles V</a> created the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Indies" title="Council of the Indies">Council of the Indies</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[Note 1]</a></sup> in 1524 as the crown entity to oversee the crown's interests in the New World. Since the time of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" title="Catholic Monarchs">Catholic Monarchs</a>, central Iberia was governed through councils appointed by the monarch with particular jurisdictions. Thus, the creation of the Council of the Indies became another, but extremely important, advisory body to the monarch.</p>
<p>The crown had set up the <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_Contrataci%C3%B3n" title="Casa de Contratación">Casa de Contratación</a> (House of Trade) in 1503 to regulate contacts between Spain and its overseas possessions. A key function was to gather information about navigation to make trips less risky and more efficient.</p>
<p>The crown under Philip II sought systematic information about his overseas empire and mandated reports, known as the <a href="/wiki/Relaciones_geogr%C3%A1ficas" title="Relaciones geográficas">Relaciones geográficas</a>, with text on topography, economic conditions, populations among other information. They were accompanied by maps of the area discussed, many of which were drawn by indigenous artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francisco_Hern%C3%A1ndez_Expedition_(1570%E2%80%9377)" title="Francisco Hernández Expedition (1570–77)">Francisco Hernández Expedition (1570–77)</a>, the first scientific expedition to the New World, was sent to gather information medicinal plants and practices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The crown created first mainland high court or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audiencia_Real" title="Audiencia Real">Audiencia</a> in 1527 to regain control of the administration of New Spain from Cortés, who as the premier conqueror of the Aztec empire, was ruling in the name of the king but without crown oversight or control. An earlier <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Audiencia_of_Santo_Domingo" title="Royal Audiencia of Santo Domingo">Audiencia</a> had been established in <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a> in 1526 to deal with the Caribbean settlements. That Audiencia, housed in the <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_las_Casas_Reales" title="Museo de las Casas Reales">Casa Reales</a> in Santo Domingo, was charged with encouraging further exploration and settlements with the authority granted it by the crown. Management by the Audiencia, which was expected to make executive decisions as a body, proved unwieldy. Therefore, in 1535, King Charles V named Don <a href="/wiki/Antonio_de_Mendoza" title="Antonio de Mendoza">Antonio de Mendoza</a> as the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroy_of_New_Spain" title="Viceroy of New Spain">Viceroy of New Spain</a>.</p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Inca_Empire" title="Spanish conquest of the Inca Empire">Spanish conquest of the Inca Empire</a> in 1532 opened up the vast territories of <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> to further conquests, the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">Crown</a> established an independent <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_Peru" title="Viceroyalty of Peru">Viceroyalty of Peru</a> there in 1540.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evangelization_in_New_Spain">Evangelization in New Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Evangelization in New Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Roman_Catholicism_in_Mexico" title="History of Roman Catholicism in Mexico">History of Roman Catholicism in Mexico</a></div>
<p>Because the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> had played such an important role in the <i><a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a></i> (Christian reconquest) of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iberian_peninsula" title="Iberian peninsula">Iberian peninsula</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a>, the Church in essence became another arm of the Spanish government. The Spanish Crown granted it a large role in the administration of the state, and this practice became even more pronounced in the New World, where prelates often assumed the role of government officials. In addition to the Church's explicit political role, the Catholic faith became a central part of Spanish identity after the conquest of last Muslim kingdom in the peninsula, the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Granada" title="Emirate of Granada">Emirate of Granada</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Alhambra_Decree" title="Alhambra Decree">expulsion of all Jews</a> who did not convert to Christianity.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistadors</a> brought with them many missionaries to promulgate the Catholic religion. Amerindians were taught the Roman Catholic religion and the language of Spain. Initially, the missionaries hoped to create a large body of Amerindian priests, but this did not come to be. Moreover, efforts were made to keep the Amerindian cultural aspects which did not violate the Catholic traditions. As an example, most Spanish priests committed themselves to learn the most important Amerindian languages (especially during the 16th century) and wrote grammars so that the missionaries could learn the languages and preach in them. This was similarly practiced by the French colonists.</p>
<p>At first, conversion seemed to be happening rapidly. The missionaries soon found that most of the natives had simply adopted "the god of the heavens", as they called the Christian god,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> as just another one of their many gods<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. While they often held the Christian god to be an important deity because it was the god of the victorious conquerors, they did not see the need to abandon their old beliefs. As a result, a second wave of missionaries began an effort to completely erase the old beliefs, which they associated with the ritualized <a href="/wiki/Human_sacrifice" title="Human sacrifice">human sacrifice</a> found in many of the native religions, eventually putting an end to this practice common before the arrival of the Spaniards. In the process many artifacts of pre-Columbian Mesoamerican culture were destroyed. Hundreds of thousands of native <a href="/wiki/Codex" title="Codex">codices</a> were burned, native priests and teachers were persecuted, and the temples and statues of the old gods were torn down. Even some foods associated with the native religions, like <a href="/wiki/Amaranth" title="Amaranth">amaranth</a>, were forbidden.</p>
<p>Many clerics, such as <a href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_de_las_Casas" title="Bartolomé de las Casas">Bartolomé de las Casas</a>, also tried to protect the natives from de facto and actual enslavement to the settlers, and obtained from the Crown decrees and promises to protect native Mesoamericans, most notably the <a href="/wiki/New_Laws" title="New Laws">New Laws</a>. Unfortunately, the royal government was too far to fully enforce them, and many abuses against the natives, even among the clergy, continued. Eventually, the Crown declared the natives to be <a href="/wiki/Ward_(law)" title="Ward (law)">legal minors</a> and placed under the guardianship of the Crown, which was responsible for their indoctrination. It was this status that barred the native population from the priesthood. During the following centuries, under Spanish rule, a new culture developed that combined the customs and traditions of the indigenous peoples with that of Catholic Spain. Numerous churches and other buildings were constructed by native labor in the Spanish style, and cities were named after various saints or religious topics such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Luis_Potos%C3%AD,_San_Luis_Potos%C3%AD" title="San Luis Potosí, San Luis Potosí">San Luis Potosí</a> (after <a href="/wiki/Louis_IX_of_France" title="Louis IX of France">Saint Louis</a>) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veracruz,_Veracruz" title="Veracruz, Veracruz">Vera Cruz</a> (the <a href="/wiki/True_Cross" title="True Cross">True Cross</a>).</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">Spanish Inquisition</a>, and its New Spanish counterpart, the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Inquisition" title="Mexican Inquisition">Mexican Inquisition</a>, continued to operate in the viceroyalty until Mexico declared its independence. During the 17th and 18th centuries, the Inquisition worked with the viceregal government to block the diffusion of <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberal</a> ideas during the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a> and the revolutionary republican and democratic ideas of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_War_of_Independence" title="United States War of Independence">United States War of Independence</a> and the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Establishment_of_Spanish_cities_in_the_early_sixteenth_century">Establishment of Spanish cities in the early sixteenth century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Establishment of Spanish cities in the early sixteenth century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coronado-Remington.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="768" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Coronado-Remington.jpg/200px-Coronado-Remington.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Coronado-Remington.jpg/300px-Coronado-Remington.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Coronado-Remington.jpg/400px-Coronado-Remington.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coronado-Remington.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"Vázquez de Coronado Sets Out to the North" (1540) by <a href="/wiki/Frederic_Remington" title="Frederic Remington">Frederic Remington</a>, oil on canvas, 1905</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish colonization of the Americas</a></div>
<p>Even before the establishment of the viceroyalty of New Spain, conquerors in central Mexico founded new Spanish cities and embarked on further conquests, a pattern that had been established in the Caribbean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> In central Mexico, the Aztec capital of <a href="/wiki/Tenochtitlan" title="Tenochtitlan">Tenochtitlan</a> was transformed into the main settlement of the territory; thus, the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mexico_City" title="History of Mexico City">history of Mexico City</a> is of huge importance to the whole colonial enterprise. Spaniards founded new settlements in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puebla_de_los_Angeles" title="Puebla de los Angeles">Puebla de los Angeles</a> (founded 1531) at the midway point between the Mexico City (founded 1521-24) and the Caribbean port of <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a> (1519). Colima (1524), <a href="/wiki/Oaxaca_City" title="Oaxaca City">Antequera</a> (1526, now Oaxaca City) and <a href="/wiki/Guadalajara" title="Guadalajara">Guadalajara</a> (1532) were all new Spanish settlements. North of Mexico City, the city of <a href="/wiki/Quer%C3%A9taro" title="Querétaro">Querétaro</a> was founded (ca. 1531) in what was called the <a href="/wiki/Baj%C3%ADo" title="Bajío">Bajío</a>, a major zone of commercial agriculture. Guadalajara was founded northwest of Mexico City (1531–42) and became the dominant Spanish settlement in the region. West of Mexico City the settlement of Valladolid (Michoacan) was founded (1529–41). In the densely indigenous South, as noted Antequera (1526) became the center of Spanish settlement in Oaxaca; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Guatemala" title="Santiago de Guatemala">Santiago de Guatemala</a> was founded in 1524; and in Yucatán, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9rida,_Yucat%C3%A1n" title="Mérida, Yucatán">Mérida</a> (1542) was founded inland, with <a href="/wiki/Campeche" title="Campeche">Campeche</a> founded as a small, Caribbean port in 1541. There was sea trade between Campeche and Veracruz.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> During the first twenty years, before the establishment of the viceroyalty, some of the important cities of the colonial era that remain important today were founded. The discovery of silver in Zacatecas in the far north was a transformative event. The settlement of <a href="/wiki/Zacatecas_City" title="Zacatecas City">Zacatecas</a> was founded in 1547 deep in the territory of the nomadic and fierce <a href="/wiki/Chichimeca" title="Chichimeca">Chichimeca</a>, whose resistance to Spanish presence was the protracted conflict of the <a href="/wiki/Chichimeca_War" title="Chichimeca War">Chichimeca War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_expansion_of_Spanish_control_on_the_mainland">Later expansion of Spanish control on the mainland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Later expansion of Spanish control on the mainland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the 16th century, many Spanish cities were established in North and Central America. Spain attempted to establish missions in what is now the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">southern United States</a> including <a href="/wiki/Spanish_missions_in_Georgia" title="Spanish missions in Georgia">Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_missions_in_the_Carolinas" title="Spanish missions in the Carolinas">South Carolina</a> between 1568 and 1587. These efforts were mainly successful in the region of present-day <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, where the city of <a href="/wiki/St._Augustine,_Florida" title="St. Augustine, Florida">St. Augustine</a> was founded in 1565, the oldest European city in the United States.</p>
<p>Upon his arrival, Viceroy Don Antonio de Mendoza vigorously took to the duties entrusted to him by the King and encouraged the exploration of Spain's new mainland territories. He commissioned the expeditions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francisco_V%C3%A1squez_de_Coronado" title="Francisco Vásquez de Coronado">Francisco Vásquez de Coronado</a> into the present day <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">American Southwest</a> in 1540–1542. The Viceroy commissioned <a href="/wiki/Juan_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Cabrillo" title="Juan Rodríguez Cabrillo">Juan Rodríguez Cabrillo</a> in the first Spanish exploration up the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> in 1542–1543. Cabrillo sailed far up the coast, becoming the first European to see present day California, United States. The Viceroy also sent <a href="/wiki/Ruy_L%C3%B3pez_de_Villalobos" title="Ruy López de Villalobos">Ruy López de Villalobos</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Spanish East Indies</a> in 1542–1543. As these new territories became controlled, they were brought under the purview of the Viceroy of New Spain.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_to_the_Philippine_Islands_and_the_Manila_trade">Expansion to the Philippine Islands and the Manila trade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Expansion to the Philippine Islands and the Manila trade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Philippines" title="History of the Philippines">History of the Philippines</a></div>
<p>Seeking to develop trade between the <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> across the Pacific Ocean, <a href="/wiki/Miguel_L%C3%B3pez_de_Legazpi" title="Miguel López de Legazpi">Miguel López de Legazpi</a> established the first Spanish settlement in the Philippine Islands in 1565, which became the town of <i>San Miguel</i> (present-day <a href="/wiki/Cebu_City" title="Cebu City">Cebu City</a>). <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_de_Urdaneta" title="Andrés de Urdaneta">Andrés de Urdaneta</a> discovered an efficient sailing route from the Philippine Islands to Mexico which took advantage of the <a href="/wiki/Kuroshio_Current" title="Kuroshio Current">Kuroshio Current</a>. In 1571, the city of <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a> became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Spanish East Indies</a>, with trade soon beginning via the <a href="/wiki/Manila_galleon" title="Manila galleon">Manila-Acapulco Galleons</a>. The Manila-Acapulco trade route shipped products such as silk, spices, silver, porcelain and gold to the Americas from Asia. The importance of the Philippines to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_empire" title="Spanish empire">Spanish empire</a> can be seen by its creation as a separate Captaincy-General.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Products brought from <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> were sent to <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a> then overland to <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a>, and then shipped to Spain aboard the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_treasure_fleet" title="Spanish treasure fleet">West Indies Fleets</a>. Later they were traded across <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_defense_against_attacks_on_shipping">Spanish defense against attacks on shipping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Spanish defense against attacks on shipping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_treasure_fleet" title="Spanish treasure fleet">Spanish treasure fleet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manila_galleon" title="Manila galleon">Manila galleon</a></div>
<p>The Spanish crown created a system of convoys of ships (called the <i>flota</i>) to prevent attacks by European privateers. Some isolated attacks on these shipments took place in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> by British and Dutch pirates and privateers. One such act of piracy was led by <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">Francis Drake</a> in 1586, and another by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cavendish" title="Thomas Cavendish">Thomas Cavendish</a> in 1587. In one episode, the cities of <a href="/wiki/Huatulco" title="Huatulco">Huatulco</a> (Oaxaca) and <a href="/wiki/Barra_de_Navidad" title="Barra de Navidad">Barra de Navidad</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jalisco" title="Jalisco">Jalisco</a> Province of México were sacked. However, these maritime routes, both across the Pacific and the Atlantic were successful in the defensive and logistical role they played in the history of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>. For over three centuries the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Navy" title="Spanish Navy">Spanish Navy</a> escorted the galleon convoys which sailed around the world.</p>
<p>Don <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lope_D%C3%ADez_de_Armend%C3%A1riz" title="Lope Díez de Armendáriz">Lope Díez de Armendáriz</a>, born in Quito, Ecuador, was the first Viceroy of New Spain who was born in the '<a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>'. He formed the 'Navy of Barlovento' <i>(Armada de Barlovento)</i>, based in Veracruz, to patrol coastal regions and protect the <a href="/wiki/Harbor" title="Harbor">harbors</a>, port towns, and trade ships from <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">pirates</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Privateers" title="Privateers">privateers</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_revolts_in_New_Spain">Internal revolts in New Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Internal revolts in New Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xochipilla.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2292" data-file-width="3056" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Xochipilla.jpg/220px-Xochipilla.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Xochipilla.jpg/330px-Xochipilla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Xochipilla.jpg/440px-Xochipilla.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Xochipilla.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Viceroy don <a href="/wiki/Antonio_de_Mendoza" title="Antonio de Mendoza">Antonio de Mendoza</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tlaxcalan" title="Tlaxcalan">Tlaxcalan</a> Indians battle with the Caxcanes in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixt%C3%B3n_war" title="Mixtón war">Mixtón war</a>, 1541-42 in Nueva Galicia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the conquest of central Mexico, there were only two major Indian revolts challenging Spanish rule. The first was in 1541, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixt%C3%B3n_war" title="Mixtón war">Mixtón war</a>, in which the viceroy himself, Don <a href="/wiki/Antonio_de_Mendoza" title="Antonio de Mendoza">Antonio de Mendoza</a> led an army against the uprising by Caxcanes. The other was the 1680 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pueblo_revolt" title="Pueblo revolt">Pueblo revolt</a>, in which Indians in 24 settlements in New Mexico expelled the Spanish who left for Texas, an exile lasting a decade. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chichimeca_war" title="Chichimeca war">Chichimeca war</a> lasted over fifty years, 1550-1606, between the Spanish and various indigenous groups of northern New Spain, particularly in silver mining regions and the transportation trunk lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> Non-sedentary or semi-sedentary Northern Indians were difficult to control once they acquired the mobility of the horse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> In 1616, the Tepehuan revolted against the Spanish, but it was relatively quickly suppressed by the Spanish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tarahumara" title="Tarahumara">Tarahumara</a> Indians were in revolt in the mountains of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chihuahua_Desert" title="Chihuahua Desert">Chihuahua</a> for several years. In 1670 <a href="/wiki/Chichimeca" title="Chichimeca">Chichimecas</a> invaded <a href="/wiki/Durango" title="Durango">Durango</a>, and the governor, Francisco González, abandoned its defense.</p>
<p>In the southern area of New Spain, the Tzeltal Maya and other indigenous groups, including the Tzotzil and Chol revolted in 1712. It was a multiethnic revolt sparked by a religious issues in several communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> In 1704 viceroy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francisco_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_la_Cueva_Enr%C3%ADquez,_10th_Duke_of_Alburquerque" title="Francisco Fernández de la Cueva Enríquez, 10th Duke of Alburquerque">Francisco Fernández de la Cueva</a> suppressed a rebellion of the <a href="/wiki/Pima_people" title="Pima people">Pima</a> Indians in <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Vizcaya,_New_Spain" title="Nueva Vizcaya, New Spain">Nueva Vizcaya</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_during_the_Habsburg_era">Economy during the Habsburg era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy during the Habsburg era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Mexico" title="Economic history of Mexico">Economic history of Mexico</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1188" data-file-width="2835" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png/350px-16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png/525px-16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png/700px-16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
White represents the route of the Manila Galleons in the Pacific and the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_treasure_fleet" title="Spanish treasure fleet">flota</a> in the Atlantic. (Blue represents <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_India_Armadas" title="Portuguese India Armadas">Portuguese routes.)</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the era of the conquest, in order to pay off the debts incurred by the conquistadors and their companies, the new Spanish governors awarded their men grants of native tribute and labor, known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encomiendas" title="Encomiendas">encomiendas</a>. In New Spain these grants were modeled after the tribute and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corvee" title="Corvee">corvee</a> labor that the <a href="/wiki/Mexica" title="Mexica">Mexica</a> rulers had demanded from native communities. This system came to signify the oppression and exploitation of natives, although its originators may not have set out with such intent. In short order the upper echelons of patrons and priests in the society lived off the work of the lower classes. Due to some horrifying instances of abuse against the indigenous peoples, Bishop <a href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_de_las_Casas" title="Bartolomé de las Casas">Bartolomé de las Casas</a> suggested bringing black slaves to replace them. Fray Bartolomé later repented when he saw the even worse treatment given to the black slaves.</p>
<p>In Peru, the other discovery that perpetuated the system of forced labor, the <a href="/wiki/Mit%27a" title="Mit'a">mit'a</a>, was the enormously rich single silver mine discovered at Potosí, but in New Spain, labor recruitment differed significantly. With the exception of silver mines worked in the Aztec period at <a href="/wiki/Taxco" title="Taxco">Taxco</a>, southwest of Tenochtitlan, the Mexico's mining region was outside the area of dense indigenous settlement. Labor for the mines in the north of Mexico had a workforce of black slave labor and indigenous wage labor, not draft labor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Altman_etal_172_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Altman_etal_172-27">[26]</a></sup> Indigenous who were drawn to the mining areas were from different regions of the center of Mexico, with a few from the north itself. With such diversity they did not have a common ethnic identity or language and rapidly assimilated to Hispanic culture. Although mining was difficult and dangerous, the wages were good, which is what drew the indigenous labor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Altman_etal_172_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Altman_etal_172-27">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Viceroyalty of New Spain was the principal source of income for Spain in the eighteenth century, with the revival of mining under the <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Reforms" title="Bourbon Reforms">Bourbon Reforms</a>. Important mining centers like <a href="/wiki/Zacatecas" title="Zacatecas">Zacatecas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guanajuato" title="Guanajuato">Guanajuato</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Luis_Potos%C3%AD" title="San Luis Potosí">San Luis Potosí</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hidalgo_(Mexico)" title="Hidalgo (Mexico)">Hidalgo</a> had been established in the sixteenth century and suffered decline for a variety of reasons in the seventeenth century, but silver mining in Mexico out performed all other Spanish overseas territories in revenues for the royal coffers.</p>
<p>The fast red dye <a href="/wiki/Cochineal" title="Cochineal">cochineal</a> was an important export in areas such as central Mexico and Oaxaca in terms of revenues to the crown and stimulation of the internal market of New Spain. <i><a href="/wiki/Chocolate" title="Chocolate">Cacao</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Indigo" title="Indigo">indigo</a> were also important exports for the New Spain, but was used through rather the vice royalties rather than contact with European countries due to piracy, and smuggling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foster_101_103_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Foster_101_103-28">[27]</a></sup> The indigo industry in particular also helped to temporarily unite communities throughout the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Guatemala" title="Kingdom of Guatemala">Kingdom of Guatemala</a> due to the smuggling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foster_101_103_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-Foster_101_103-28">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>There were two major ports in New Spain, <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a> the viceroyalty's principal port on the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a> on the Pacific, terminus of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manila_Galleon" title="Manila Galleon">Manila Galleon</a>. In the Philippines <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a> near the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> was the main port. The ports were fundamental for overseas trade, stretching a trade route from Asia, through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manila_Galleon" title="Manila Galleon">Manila Galleon</a> to the Spanish mainland.</p>
<p>These were ships that made voyages from the Philippines to Mexico, whose goods were then transported overland from Acapulco to Veracruz and later reshipped from Veracruz to <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a> in Spain. So then, the ships that set sail from Veracruz were generally loaded with merchandise from the East Indies originating from the commercial centers of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, plus the <a href="/wiki/Precious_metal" title="Precious metal">precious metals</a> and natural resources of Mexico, Central America, and the Caribbean. During the 16th century, Spain held the equivalent of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USD" title="USD">US$</a>1.5 trillion (1990 terms) in <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> and silver received from New Spain.</p>
<p>However, these resources did not translate into development for the <a href="/wiki/Metropolis" title="Metropolis">Metropolis</a> (mother country) due to Spanish Roman Catholic Monarchy's frequent preoccupation with European wars (enormous amounts of this wealth were spent hiring mercenaries to fight the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a>), as well as the incessant decrease in overseas transportation caused by assaults from companies of British <a href="/wiki/Buccaneer" title="Buccaneer">buccaneers</a>, Dutch <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">corsairs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">pirates</a> of various origin. These companies were initially financed by, at first, by the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> <a href="/wiki/Stock_market" title="Stock market">stock market</a>, the first in history and whose origin is owed precisely to the need for funds to finance pirate expeditions, as later by the London market. The above is what some authors call the "historical process of the transfer of wealth from the south to the north."</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Bourbon_reforms_.281713.E2.80.931806.29">The Bourbon reforms (1713–1806)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: The Bourbon reforms (1713–1806)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Reforms" title="Bourbon Reforms">Bourbon Reforms</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jos%C3%A9_de_G%C3%A1lvez.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="504" data-file-width="372" height="298" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Jos%C3%A9_de_G%C3%A1lvez.jpg/220px-Jos%C3%A9_de_G%C3%A1lvez.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Jos%C3%A9_de_G%C3%A1lvez.jpg/330px-Jos%C3%A9_de_G%C3%A1lvez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9c/Jos%C3%A9_de_G%C3%A1lvez.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

José de Gálvez, marqués de Sonora, Visitador in New Spain, who initiated major reforms.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CarlosFranciscodeCroix.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="624" data-file-width="480" height="286" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/CarlosFranciscodeCroix.jpg/220px-CarlosFranciscodeCroix.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/CarlosFranciscodeCroix.jpg/330px-CarlosFranciscodeCroix.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/CarlosFranciscodeCroix.jpg/440px-CarlosFranciscodeCroix.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
