<a href="/wiki/Carlos_Francisco_de_Croix,_marqu%C3%A9s_de_Croix" title="Carlos Francisco de Croix, marqués de Croix">Carlos Francisco de Croix, marqués de Croix</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroy_of_New_Spain" title="Viceroy of New Spain">Viceroy of New Spain</a> (1766-1771)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AntonioMariadeBucareliyUrsua.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="597" data-file-width="480" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/AntonioMariadeBucareliyUrsua.jpg/220px-AntonioMariadeBucareliyUrsua.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/AntonioMariadeBucareliyUrsua.jpg/330px-AntonioMariadeBucareliyUrsua.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/AntonioMariadeBucareliyUrsua.jpg/440px-AntonioMariadeBucareliyUrsua.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AntonioMariadeBucareliyUrsua.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Antonio_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Bucareli_y_Urs%C3%BAa" title="Antonio María de Bucareli y Ursúa">Antonio María de Bucareli y Ursúa</a>, marqués de Valleheroso y conde de Jerena, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroy_of_New_Spain" title="Viceroy of New Spain">Viceroy of New Spain</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JuanVicentedeGuemesPachecoyPadilla.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="660" data-file-width="480" height="303" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/JuanVicentedeGuemesPachecoyPadilla.jpg/220px-JuanVicentedeGuemesPachecoyPadilla.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/JuanVicentedeGuemesPachecoyPadilla.jpg/330px-JuanVicentedeGuemesPachecoyPadilla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/JuanVicentedeGuemesPachecoyPadilla.jpg/440px-JuanVicentedeGuemesPachecoyPadilla.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JuanVicentedeGuemesPachecoyPadilla.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Juan Vicente de Güemes Padilla Horcasitas y Aguayo, 2nd <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Revilla_Gigedo" title="Count of Revilla Gigedo">Count of Revillagigedo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroy_of_New_Spain" title="Viceroy of New Spain">Viceroy of New Spain</a> (1789-1794)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Bourbon monarchy embarked upon a far-reaching program to revitalize the economy of its territories, both on the peninsula and its overseas possessions, to enhance administrative efficiency and crown control, and to decrease the power and privilege of the Roman Catholic Church vis-a-vis the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>The British capture and occupation of both Manila and Havana in 1762 during the global conflict of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> meant that the Spanish crown had to rethink its military strategy for defending its possessions. The Spanish crown had engaged with Britain for a number of years in low intensity warfare, with ports and trade routes harassed by English privateers. The crown strengthened the defenses of <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_de_Ul%C3%BAa" title="San Juan de Ulúa">San Juan de Ulúa</a>, Jamaica, Cuba, and Florida, but the British sacked ports in the late seventeenth century.<a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Cuba" title="Santiago de Cuba">Santiago de Cuba</a> (1662), <a href="/wiki/St._Augustine,_Florida" title="St. Augustine, Florida">St. Augustine</a> <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Spanish Florida</a> (1665) and <a href="/wiki/Campeche" title="Campeche">Campeche</a> 1678 and so with the loss of Havana and Manila, Spain realized it needed to take significant steps. The Bourbons created a standing army in New Spain, beginning in 1764, and strengthened defensive infrastructure, such as forts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>The crown sought reliable information about New Spain and dispatched <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_G%C3%A1lvez" title="José de Gálvez">José de Gálvez</a> as <i>Visitador General</i> (inspector general), who observed conditions needing reform, starting in 1765, in order to strengthen crown control over the kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>An important feature of the Bourbon Reforms was that they ended the significant amount of local control that was a characteristic of the bureaucracy under the Habsburgs, especially through the sale of offices. The Bourbons sought a return to the monarchical ideal of having those not directly connected with local elites as administrators, who in theory should be disinterested, staff the higher echelons of regional government. In practice this meant that there was a concerted effort to appoint mostly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peninsulares" title="Peninsulares">peninsulares</a>, usually military men with long records of service (as opposed to the Habsburg preference for prelates), who were willing to move around the global empire. The intendancies were one new office that could be staffed with peninsulares, but throughout the 18th century significant gains were made in the numbers of governors-captain generals, audiencia judges and bishops, in addition to other posts, who were Spanish-born.</p>
<p>In 1766, the crown appointed <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Francisco_de_Croix,_marqu%C3%A9s_de_Croix" title="Carlos Francisco de Croix, marqués de Croix">Carlos Francisco de Croix, marqués de Croix</a> as viceroy of New Spain. One of his early tasks was to implement the crown's decision to expel the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuits" title="Jesuits">Jesuits</a> from all its territories, accomplished in 1767. Since the Jesuits had significant power, owning large, well managed haciendas, educating New Spain's elite young men, and as a religious order resistant to crown control, the Jesuits were a major target for the assertion of crown control. Croix closed the religious autos-de-fe of the Holy Office of the Inquisition to public viewing, signaling a shift in the crown's attitude toward religion. Other significant accomplishments under Croix's administration was the founding of the College of Surgery in 1768, part of the crown's push to introduce institutional reforms that regulated professions. The crown was also interested in generating more income for its coffers and Croix instituted the royal lottery in 1769. Croix also initiated improvements in the capital and seat of the viceroyalty, increasing the size of its central park, the Alameda.</p>
<p>Another activist viceroy carrying out reforms was <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Bucareli_y_Urs%C3%BAa" title="Antonio María de Bucareli y Ursúa">Antonio María de Bucareli y Ursúa</a>, marqués de Valleheroso y conde de Jerena, who served from 1771 to 1779, and died in office. José de Gálvez, now Minister of the Indies following his appointment as Visitor General of New Spain, briefed the newly appointed viceroy about reforms to be implemented. In 1776, a new northern territorial division was established, <a href="/wiki/Provincias_Internas" title="Provincias Internas">Commandancy General of the Provincias Internas</a> known as the <i>Provincias Internas</i> (Commandancy General of the Internal Provinces of the North, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span lang="es"><i>Comandancia y Capitanía General de las Provincias Internas</i></span>). <a href="/wiki/Teodoro_de_Croix" title="Teodoro de Croix">Teodoro de Croix</a> (nephew of the former viceroy) was appointed the first Commander General of the Provincias Internas, independent of the Viceroy of New Spain, to provide better administration for the northern frontier provinces. They included <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Vizcaya,_New_Spain" title="Nueva Vizcaya, New Spain">Nueva Vizcaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_Santander" title="Nuevo Santander">Nuevo Santander</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sonora_y_Sinaloa" title="Sonora y Sinaloa">Sonora y Sinaloa</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Californias" title="Las Californias">Las Californias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coahuila_y_Tejas" title="Coahuila y Tejas">Coahuila y Tejas</a> (Coahuila and Texas), and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico" title="Santa Fe de Nuevo México">Nuevo México</a>. Bucareli was opposed to Gálvez's plan to implement the new administrative organization of intendancies, which he believed would burden areas with sparse population with excessive costs for the new bureaucracy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>The new Bourbon kings did not split the Viceroyalty of New Spain into smaller administrative units as they did with the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_Peru" title="Viceroyalty of Peru">Viceroyalty of Peru</a>, carving out the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" title="Viceroyalty of Río de la Plata">Viceroyalty of Río de la Plata</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of New Granada">Viceroyalty of New Granada</a>, but New Spain was reorganized administratively and elite American-born Spanish men were passed over for high office. The crown also established a standing military, with the aim of defending its overseas territories.</p>
<p>The Spanish Bourbons monarchs' prime innovation introduction of <a href="/wiki/Intendant" title="Intendant">intendancies</a>, an institution emulating that of Bourbon France. They were first introduced on a large scale in New Spain, by the Minister of the Indies <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_G%C3%A1lvez" title="José de Gálvez">José de Gálvez</a>, in the 1770s, who originally envisioned that they would replace the viceregal system (viceroyalty) altogether. With broad powers over tax collection and the public treasury and with a mandate to help foster economic growth over their districts, intendants encroached on the traditional powers of viceroys, governors and local officials, such as the <a href="/wiki/Corregidor" title="Corregidor">corregidores</a>, which were phased out as intendancies were established. The Crown saw the intendants as a check on these other officers. Over time accommodations were made. For example, after a period of experimentation in which an independent intendant was assigned to Mexico City, the office was thereafter given to the same person who simultaneously held the post of viceroy. Nevertheless, the creation of scores of autonomous intendancies throughout the Viceroyalty, created a great deal of decentralization, and in the <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Guatemala" title="Captaincy General of Guatemala">Captaincy General of Guatemala</a>, in particular, the intendancy laid the groundwork for the future independent nations of the 19th century. In 1780, Minister of the Indies <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_G%C3%A1lvez" title="José de Gálvez">José de Gálvez</a> sent a royal dispatch to <a href="/wiki/Teodoro_de_Croix" title="Teodoro de Croix">Teodoro de Croix</a>, Commandant General of the Internal Provinces of New Spain <i>(Provincias Internas)</i>, asking all subjects to donate money to help the American Revolution. Millions of pesos were given.</p>
<p>The focus on the economy (and the revenues it provided to the royal coffers) was also extended to society at large. Economic associations were promoted, such as the <a href="/wiki/Sociedad_Econ%C3%B3mica_de_los_Amigos_del_Pa%C3%ADs" title="Sociedad Económica de los Amigos del País">Economic Society of Friends of the Country</a>. Similar "Friends of the Country" economic societies were established throughout the Spanish world, including Cuba and Guatemala.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>The crown sent a series of scientific expeditions to its overseas possessions, including the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Botanical_Expedition_to_New_Spain" title="Royal Botanical Expedition to New Spain">Royal Botanical Expedition to New Spain</a>, led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_de_Sess%C3%A9" title="Martín de Sessé">Martín de Sessé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mariano_Moci%C3%B1o" title="José Mariano Mociño">José Mariano Mociño</a> (1787-1808).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Bourbon Reforms were not a unified or entirely coherent program, but a series of crown initiatives designed to revitalize the economies of its overseas possessions and make administration more efficient and firmly under control of the crown. Record keeping improved and records were more centralized. The bureaucracy was staffed with well-qualified men, most of them peninsular-born Spaniards. The preference for them meant that there was resentment from American-born elite men and their families, who were excluded from holding office. The creation of a military meant that some American Spaniards became officers in local militias, but the ranks were filled with poor, mixed-race men, who resented service and avoided it if possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_century_military_conflicts">18th century military conflicts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 18th century military conflicts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_Spain)" title="Louisiana (New Spain)">Louisiana (New Spain)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_de_cuera.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1565" data-file-width="1799" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Dragon_de_cuera.jpg/220px-Dragon_de_cuera.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Dragon_de_cuera.jpg/330px-Dragon_de_cuera.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Dragon_de_cuera.jpg/440px-Dragon_de_cuera.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_de_cuera.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
18th-century <i><a href="/wiki/Soldado_de_cuera" title="Soldado de cuera">soldado de cuera</a></i> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonial_Mexico" title="Colonial Mexico">colonial Mexico</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first century that saw the Bourbons on the <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spanish</a> throne coincided with series of <a href="/wiki/Second_Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Second Hundred Years' War">global conflicts</a> that pitted primarily France against Great Britain. Spain as an ally of Bourbon France was drawn into these conflicts. In fact part of the motivation for the Bourbon Reforms was the perceived need to prepare the empire administratively, economically and militarily for what was the next expected war. The <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> proved to be catalyst for most of the reforms in the overseas possessions, just like the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a> had been for the reforms on the Peninsula.</p>
<p>In 1720, the <a href="/wiki/Villasur_expedition" title="Villasur expedition">Villasur expedition</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Province_of_New_Mexico,_Mexico" title="Province of New Mexico, Mexico">Santa Fe</a> met and attempted to parley with <a href="/wiki/French_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="French colonization of the Americas">French</a>- allied <a href="/wiki/Pawnee_people" title="Pawnee people">Pawnee</a> in what is now <a href="/wiki/Nebraska" title="Nebraska">Nebraska</a>. Negotiations were unsuccessful, and a battle ensued; the Spanish were badly defeated, with only thirteen managing to return to New Mexico. Although this was a small engagement, it is significant in that it was the deepest penetration of the Spanish into the <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a>, establishing the limit to Spanish expansion and influence there.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_of_Jenkin%27s_Ear" title="War of Jenkin's Ear">War of Jenkin's Ear</a> broke out in 1739 between the Spanish and British and was confined to the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Georgia" title="Province of Georgia">Georgia</a>. The major action in the War of Jenkins' Ear was a major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amphibious_attack" title="Amphibious attack">amphibious attack</a> launched by the British under Admiral <a href="/wiki/Edward_Vernon" title="Edward Vernon">Edward Vernon</a> in March 1741 against <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cartagena_de_Indias" title="Battle of Cartagena de Indias">Cartagena de Indias</a>, one of Spain's major gold-trading ports in the Caribbean (today <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>). Although this episode is largely forgotten, it ended in a decisive victory for Spain, who managed to prolong its control of the Caribbean and indeed secure the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Main" title="Spanish Main">Spanish Main</a> until the 19th century.</p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a>/<a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>, the British troops invaded and captured the Spanish cities of <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a> in the Philippines in 1762. The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris (1763)</a> gave Spain control over the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">Louisiana</a> part of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> including <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a>, creating a Spanish empire that stretched from the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> to the Pacific Ocean; but Spain also ceded <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Florida</a> to <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> in order to regain Cuba, which the British occupied during the war. Louisiana settlers, hoping to restore the territory to France, in the bloodless <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rebellion_of_1768" title="Rebellion of 1768">Rebellion of 1768</a> forced the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louisiana_Governor" title="Louisiana Governor">Louisiana Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Antonio_de_Ulloa" title="Antonio de Ulloa">Antonio de Ulloa</a> to flee to Spain. The rebellion was crushed in 1769 by the next governor <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_O%27Reilly" title="Alejandro O'Reilly">Alejandro O'Reilly</a>, who executed five of the conspirators. The Louisiana territory was to be administered by superiors in Cuba with a governor on site in New Orleans.</p>
<p>The 21 northern <a href="/wiki/Spanish_missions_in_California#Missions_in_present-day_California_.28U.S..29" title="Spanish missions in California">missions in present-day California</a> (U.S.) were established along California's <a href="/wiki/El_Camino_Real_(California)" title="El Camino Real (California)">El Camino Real</a> from 1769. In an effort to exclude <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Britain</a> and Russia from the eastern Pacific, King <a href="/wiki/Charles_III_of_Spain" title="Charles III of Spain">Charles III of Spain</a> sent forth from Mexico a number of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_expeditions_to_the_Pacific_Northwest" title="Spanish expeditions to the Pacific Northwest">expeditions to the Pacific Northwest</a> between 1774 and 1793. Spain's long-held claims and navigation rights were strengthened and a settlement and fort were built in <a href="/wiki/Nootka_Sound" title="Nootka Sound">Nootka Sound</a>, Alaska.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spanish_troops_at_Pensacola.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="680" data-file-width="643" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Spanish_troops_at_Pensacola.jpg/220px-Spanish_troops_at_Pensacola.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Spanish_troops_at_Pensacola.jpg/330px-Spanish_troops_at_Pensacola.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Spanish_troops_at_Pensacola.jpg/440px-Spanish_troops_at_Pensacola.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spanish_troops_at_Pensacola.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Spanish army defeats British soldiers in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pensacola_(1781)" title="Battle of Pensacola (1781)">Battle of Pensacola</a> in 1781. In 1783 the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">Treaty of Paris</a> returns all of <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> to Spain for the return of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Spain entered the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a> as an ally of France in June 1779, a renewal of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bourbon_Family_Compact" title="Bourbon Family Compact">Bourbon Family Compact</a>. In 1781, a Spanish expedition during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a> left <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" title="St. Louis, Missouri">St. Louis, Missouri</a>, (then under Spanish control) and reached as far as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_St._Joseph_(Niles)" title="Fort St. Joseph (Niles)">Fort St. Joseph</a> at <a href="/wiki/Niles,_Michigan" title="Niles, Michigan">Niles, Michigan</a>, where they captured the fort while the British were away. On 8 May 1782, Count <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bernardo_de_G%C3%A1lvez_y_Madrid,_Count_of_G%C3%A1lvez" title="Bernardo de Gálvez y Madrid, Count of Gálvez">Bernardo de Gálvez</a>, the Spanish governor of <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_Spain)" title="Louisiana (New Spain)">Louisiana</a>, captured the British naval base at <a href="/wiki/New_Providence" title="New Providence">New Providence</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">the Bahamas</a>. On the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast" title="Gulf Coast">Gulf Coast</a>, the military actions of Gálvez led to Spain's re-acquisition of <a href="/wiki/East_Florida" title="East Florida">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Florida" title="West Florida">West Florida</a> in the peace settlement, as well as controlling the <a href="/wiki/River_mouth" title="River mouth">mouth</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> after the war — which would prove to be a major source of tension between Spain and the United States in the years to come.</p>
<p>In the second <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">Treaty of Paris (1783)</a>, which ended the American Revolution, Britain ceded its two Florida colonies back to Spain to regain the Bahamas, which Spain had been occupying during the war. Spain then had control over the Mississippi River south of 32°30' north latitude, and, in what is known as the Spanish Conspiracy, hoped to gain greater control of Louisiana and all of the west. These hopes ended when Spain was pressured into signing <a href="/wiki/Pinckney%27s_Treaty" title="Pinckney's Treaty">Pinckney's Treaty</a> in 1795. France reacquired 'Louisiana' from Spain in the secret <a href="/wiki/Third_Treaty_of_San_Ildefonso" title="Third Treaty of San Ildefonso">Treaty of San Ildefonso</a> in 1800. The United States bought the territory from France in the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana Purchase</a> of 1803.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NutcaEN.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="931" data-file-width="1103" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/NutcaEN.png/220px-NutcaEN.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/NutcaEN.png/330px-NutcaEN.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/NutcaEN.png/440px-NutcaEN.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NutcaEN.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Spanish territorial claims in the West Coast of North America, 18th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>New Spain claimed the entire west coast of North America and therefore considered the Russian fur trading activity in Alaska, which began in the middle to late 18th century, an encroachment and threat. Likewise, the exploration of the northwest coast by Captain <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> of the British Navy and the subsequent fur trading activities by British ships was considered an encroachment on Spanish territory. To protect and strengthen its claim, New Spain sent a number of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_expeditions_to_the_Pacific_Northwest" title="Spanish expeditions to the Pacific Northwest">expeditions to the Pacific Northwest</a> between 1774 and 1793. In 1789 a naval outpost called <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Nuca" title="Santa Cruz de Nuca">Santa Cruz de Nuca</a> (or just Nuca) was established at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Friendly_Cove" title="Friendly Cove">Friendly Cove</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nootka_Sound" title="Nootka Sound">Nootka Sound</a> (now Yuquot), <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Island" title="Vancouver Island">Vancouver Island</a>. It was protected by an <a href="/wiki/Artillery_battery" title="Artillery battery">artillery</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_battery" title="Land battery">land battery</a> called <a href="/wiki/Fort_San_Miguel" title="Fort San Miguel">Fort San Miguel</a>. Santa Cruz de Nuca was the northernmost establishment of New Spain. It was the first European colony in what is now the province of <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a> and the only Spanish settlement in what is now <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. Santa Cruz de Nuca remained under the control of New Spain until 1795, when it was abandoned under the terms of the third <a href="/wiki/Nootka_Convention" title="Nootka Convention">Nootka Convention</a>. Another outpost, intended to replace Santa Cruz de Nuca, was partially built at <a href="/wiki/Neah_Bay,_Washington" title="Neah Bay, Washington">Neah Bay</a> on the southern side of the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Juan_de_Fuca" title="Strait of Juan de Fuca">Strait of Juan de Fuca</a> in what is now the <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>. Neah Bay was known as <i>Bahía de Núñez Gaona</i> in New Spain, and the outpost there was referred to as "Fuca". It was abandoned, partially finished, in 1792. Its personnel, livestock, cannons, and ammunition were transferred to Nuca.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1789, at Santa Cruz de Nuca, a conflict occurred between the Spanish naval officer <a href="/wiki/Esteban_Jos%C3%A9_Mart%C3%ADnez_Fern%C3%A1ndez_y_Mart%C3%ADnez_de_la_Sierra" title="Esteban José Martínez Fernández y Martínez de la Sierra">Esteban José Martínez</a> and the British merchant <a href="/wiki/James_Colnett" title="James Colnett">James Colnett</a>, triggering the <a href="/wiki/Nootka_Crisis" title="Nootka Crisis">Nootka Crisis</a>, which grew into an <a href="/wiki/International_incident" title="International incident">international incident</a> and the threat of war between Britain and Spain. The first <a href="/wiki/Nootka_Convention" title="Nootka Convention">Nootka Convention</a> averted the war but left many specific issues unresolved. Both sides sought to define a northern boundary for New Spain. At Nootka Sound, the diplomatic representative of New Spain, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Francisco_de_la_Bodega_y_Quadra" title="Juan Francisco de la Bodega y Quadra">Juan Francisco de la Bodega y Quadra</a>, proposed a boundary at the Strait of Juan de Fuca, but the British representative, <a href="/wiki/George_Vancouver" title="George Vancouver">George Vancouver</a> refused to accept any boundary north of <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>. No agreement could be reached and the northern boundary of New Spain remained unspecified until the <a href="/wiki/Adams%E2%80%93On%C3%ADs_Treaty" title="Adams–Onís Treaty">Adams–Onís Treaty</a> with the United States (1819). That treaty also ceded <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Spanish Florida</a> to the United States.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_the_Viceroyalty_.281806.E2.80.931821.29">End of the Viceroyalty (1806–1821)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: End of the Viceroyalty (1806–1821)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Third_Treaty_of_San_Ildefonso" title="Third Treaty of San Ildefonso">Third Treaty of San Ildefonso</a> ceded to France the vast territory that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon</a> then sold to the United States, known as the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana Purchase</a> (1803). <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Spanish Florida</a> followed in 1819.</p>
<p>In the 1821 <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_of_the_Mexican_Empire" title="Declaration of Independence of the Mexican Empire">Declaration of Independence of the Mexican Empire</a>, both Mexico and Central America declared their independence after three centuries of Spanish rule and formed the <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Empire" title="First Mexican Empire">First Mexican Empire</a>, although Central America quickly rejected the union. After priest <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Hidalgo_y_Costilla" title="Miguel Hidalgo y Costilla">Miguel Hidalgo y Costilla</a>'s 1810 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grito_de_Dolores" title="Grito de Dolores">Grito de Dolores</a> (call for independence), the insurgent army began an eleven-year war. At first, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Criollo_class" title="Criollo class">Criollo class</a> fought against the rebels. But in 1820, a military coup in Spain forced Ferdinand VII to accept the authority of the liberal <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1812" title="Spanish Constitution of 1812">Spanish Constitution</a>. The specter of liberalism that could undermine the authority and autonomy of the Roman Catholic Church made the Church hierarchy in New Spain view independence in a different light. In an independent nation, the Church anticipated retaining its power. Royalist military officer <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%ADn_de_Iturbide" title="Agustín de Iturbide">Agustín de Iturbide</a> proposed uniting with the insurgents with whom he had battled, and gained the alliance of <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Guerrero" title="Vicente Guerrero">Vicente Guerrero</a>, leader of the insurgents in a region now bearing his name. Royal government collapsed in New Spain and the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Three_Guarantees" title="Army of the Three Guarantees">Army of the Three Guarantees</a> marched triumphantly into Mexico City in 1821.</p>
<p>The new <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Empire" title="First Mexican Empire">Mexican Empire</a> offered the crown to <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">Ferdinand VII</a> or to a member of the Spanish royal family that he would designate. After the refusal of the Spanish monarchy to recognize the independence of Mexico, the <i><span lang="es">ejército Trigarante</span></i> (<a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Three_Guarantees" title="Army of the Three Guarantees">Army of the Three Guarantees</a>), led by Agustín de Iturbide and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vincente_Guerrero" title="Vincente Guerrero">Vincente Guerrero</a>, cut all political and economic ties with Spain and crowned Iturbide as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Emperors_of_Mexico" title="List of Emperors of Mexico">emperor Agustín of Mexico</a>. Central America was originally planned to be part of the Mexican Empire; but it seceded peacefully in 1823, forming the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Federal Republic of Central America">United Provinces of Central America</a> under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitution_of_1824" title="Constitution of 1824">Constitution of 1824</a>.</p>
<p>This left only <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_West_Indies" title="Spanish West Indies">Spanish West Indies</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Spanish East Indies</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>) in the Spanish Empire; until their loss to the United States in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a> (1898).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_organization">Political organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Political organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Viceroyalty of New Spain united many regions and provinces of the Spanish Empire throughout half a world. These included on the North American mainland, central Mexico, <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Extremadura" title="Nueva Extremadura">Nueva Extremadura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Galicia" title="Nueva Galicia">Nueva Galicia</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Californias" title="The Californias">the Californias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Vizcaya,_New_Spain" title="Nueva Vizcaya, New Spain">Nueva Vizcaya</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuevo_Reyno_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Nuevo Reyno de León">Nuevo Reyno de León</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Texas" title="Spanish Texas">Texas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_Santander" title="Nuevo Santander">Nuevo Santander</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Guatemala" title="Captaincy General of Guatemala">Captaincy General of Guatemala</a>.</p>
<p>In the Caribbean it included Cuba, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colony_of_Santo_Domingo" title="Colony of Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a>, most of the <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuelan mainland</a> and the other islands in the Caribbean controlled by the Spanish. In Asia, the Viceroyalty ruled the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Captaincy General of the Philippines</a>, which covered all of the Spanish territories in the Asia-Pacific region. The outpost at Nootka Sound, on <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Island" title="Vancouver Island">Vancouver Island</a>, was considered part of the province of California.</p>
<p>Therefore, the Viceroyalty's former territories included what is now the present day countries of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>; the United States regions of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">Mariana Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>; a portion of the Canadian province of <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>; the Caribbean nations of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, the island of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>; the Asia-Pacific nations of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippine Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">Caroline Islands</a>.</p>
<p>The Viceroyalty was administered by a <a href="/wiki/Viceroy" title="Viceroy">viceroy</a> residing in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> and appointed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_monarchy" title="Spanish monarchy">Spanish monarch</a>, who had administrative oversight of all of these regions, although most matters were handled by the local governmental bodies, which ruled the various regions of the viceroyalty. First among these were the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audiencia_Real" title="Audiencia Real">audiencias</a>, which were primarily superior tribunals, but which also had administrative and legislative functions. Each of these was responsible to the Viceroy of New Spain in administrative matters (though not in judicial ones), but they also answered directly to the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Indies" title="Council of the Indies">Council of the Indies</a>.</p>
<p>Audiencia districts further incorporated the older, smaller divisions known as <a href="/wiki/Governorate" title="Governorate">governorates</a> (<i>gobernaciones</i>, roughly equivalent to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Provinces" title="Provinces">provinces</a>), which had been originally established by conquistador-governors known as <i><a href="/wiki/Adelantado" title="Adelantado">adelantados</a></i>. Provinces, which were under military threat, were grouped into <a href="/wiki/Captaincy" title="Captaincy">captaincies general</a>, such as the Captaincies General of the Philippines (established 1574) and Guatemala (established in 1609) mentioned above, which were joint military and political commands with a certain level of autonomy. (The viceroy was captain-general of those provinces that remained directly under his command).</p>
<p>At the local level there were over two hundred districts, in both Indian and Spanish areas, which were headed by either a <i><a href="/wiki/Corregidor_(position)" title="Corregidor (position)">corregidor</a></i> (also known as an <i>alcalde mayor</i>) or a <i><a href="/wiki/Cabildo_(council)" title="Cabildo (council)">cabildo</a></i> (town council), both of which had judicial and administrative powers. In the late 18th century the Bourbon dynasty began phasing out the <i>corregidores</i> and introduced <a href="/wiki/Intendant" title="Intendant">intendants</a>, whose broad fiscal powers cut into the authority of the viceroys, governors and <i>cabildos</i>. Despite their late creation, these intendancies so affected the formation of regional identity that they became the basis for the nations of Central America and the first Mexican states after independence.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Audiencias">Audiencias</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Audiencias">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Audiencia_of_Mexico" title="Royal Audiencia of Mexico">Royal Audiencia of Mexico</a></div>
<p>The high courts or audiencias were established in major areas of Spanish settlement. In New Spain the high court was established in 1527, prior to the establishment of the viceroyalty. The First Audiencia was headed by <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hernán Cortés">Hernán Cortés</a>'s rival <a href="/wiki/Nu%C3%B1o_de_Guzm%C3%A1n" title="Nuño de Guzmán">Nuño de Guzmán</a>, who used the court to deprive Cortés of power and property. The First Audiencia was dissolved and the Second Audiencia established.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Audiencias with dates of creation:</p>
<p><b>1.</b> <a href="/wiki/Real_Audiencia_of_Santo_Domingo" title="Real Audiencia of Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a> (1511, effective 1526, predated the Viceroyalty)<br/>
<b>2.</b> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Audiencia_of_Mexico" title="Real Audiencia of Mexico">Mexico</a> (1527, predated the Viceroyalty)<br/>
<b>3.</b> <a href="/wiki/Real_Audiencia_of_Panama" title="Real Audiencia of Panama">Panama</a> (1st one, 1538–1543)<br/>
<b>4.</b> <a href="/wiki/Real_Audiencia_of_Guatemala" title="Real Audiencia of Guatemala">Guatemala</a> (1543)<br/>
<b>5.</b> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Audiencia_of_Guadalajara" title="Real Audiencia of Guadalajara">Guadalajara</a> (1548)<br/>
<b>6.</b> <a href="/wiki/Real_Audiencia_of_Manila" title="Real Audiencia of Manila">Manila</a> (1583)</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Autonomous_captaincies_general">Autonomous captaincies general</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Autonomous captaincies general">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With dates of creation:</p>
<p><b>1.</b> <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Santo_Domingo" title="Captaincy General of Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a> (1535)<br/></p>
<p><b>2.</b> <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Philippines</a> (1574)<br/></p>
<p><b>3.</b> <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Captaincy General of Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> (1580)<br/></p>
<p><b>4.</b> <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Cuba" title="Captaincy General of Cuba">Cuba</a> (1607)<br/>
- which included <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Spanish Florida</a>, or <i>La Florida</i>, in North America</p>
<p><b>5.</b> <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Guatemala" title="Captaincy General of Guatemala">Guatemala</a> (1609)<br/></p>
<p><b>6.</b> <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Yucat%C3%A1n" title="Captaincy General of Yucatán">Yucatán</a> (1617)</p>
<p><b>7.</b> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commandancy_General_of_the_Provincias_Internas" title="Commandancy General of the Provincias Internas">Commandancy General of the Provincias Internas</a> (1776) (Analogous to a dependent captaincy general.)</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Intendancies">Intendancies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Intendancies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As part of the sweeping eighteenth-century administrative and economic changes known as the <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Reforms" title="Bourbon Reforms">Bourbon Reforms</a>, the Spanish crown created new administrative units called intendancies. In New Spain, these units generally corresponded to the regions or provinces that had developed earlier in the Center, South, and North. In turn, many of the intendancy boundaries became Mexican state boundaries after independence.</p>
